  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f3de8702-c171-424a-8478-d8767dc5cf78'

  <span id="freeText7183234708881460345" style="display:none">They say Delia burned herself to death in her stepfather’s shed. They say it was suicide.<br /><br />But June doesn’t believe it.<br /><br />June and Delia used to be closer than anything. Best friends in that way that comes before everyone else—before guys, before family. It was like being in love, but more. They had a billion secrets, binding them together like thin silk cords.<br /><br />But one night a year ago, everything changed. June, Delia, and June’s boyfriend Ryan were just having a little fun. Their good time got out of hand. And in the cold blue light of morning, June knew only this—things would never be the same again.<br /><br />And now, a year later, Delia is dead. June is certain she was murdered. And she owes it to her to find out the truth…which is far more complicated than she ever could have imagined.<br /><br />Sexy, dark, and atmospheric, <i>Suicide Notes from Beautiful Girls</i> will keep you guessing until the very last page.</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/576063-i-just-finished-this-book-i-liked-it">I just finished this book. I liked it much more than I thought I would. I&#39;m a little unclear about the end though. I think I know what happened, but would like to know other people&#39;s thoughts about it. So, what does everyone think?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_576063'><a id="like_count_community_question_576063" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/576063?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">2 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F18244970-suicide-notes-from-beautiful-girls">like</a></span>

</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/46215333-stephanie-fintel"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1471313661i/46215333._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/46215333-stephanie-fintel">Stephanie Fintel</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I had to read the ending twice to really grasp it. The morning June wakes up at the house after getting drunk and having sex with Sebastian, Delia and<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I had to read the ending twice to really grasp it. The morning June wakes up at the house after getting drunk and having sex with Sebastian, Delia and Ashling go on a couple "errands". later we find out these errands included Delia and Ashling tampering with Jeremiah's car which lead to his death in order to protect June from his suspicions that she killed Delia, and I think also during this time Ashling wrote the fake suicide note for William forging his handwriting. Evan, Sebastian and Ashling knew the goal was to kill William and they also knew June didn't know the truth. Sebastian almost told June the truth when she was eating pancakes that morning but was interrupted by Evan coming into the room. As far as the rape goes I believe we are to assume Delia lied about this. When William was dying he and Delia looked June in the face and she thought to herself she knew without a doubt who was lying and she left the room and then was so bothered by what happened she couldn't look at Delia or be around her. June hated her house more than any other place but at that moment after William died she would rather be at her house than around Delia and the others. June wanted to see the best in Delia so she went back to the house at 5 am for answers about Jeremiah and William even though she already knew the truth, she needed Delia to either admit it or deny it to her face. Delia was obsessed with June from the moment she laid eyes on her. She trapped June into this moment at the end. June had literally no choice except to go with Delia and the others. They all decided June needed to leave with them without talking to June about it. Delia thought for sure June came back because she WANTED to stay with Delia and run away with them leaving everything behind. When Delia realized June was not wanting to go with her she revealed the gun she stole from Tig. She admits to originally stealing it to kill herself with but now she is using it to threaten June. She is telling June she has two choices, June can leave with Delia and the rest and fake a suicide like the others, or Delia will kill her because Delia will not allow June to leave her ever again. June is very weak, scared, and fragile and throughout the book she will do whatever Delia wants or asks with no second thought. Because of this and due to the obviously fake suicide note I believe June allowed herself to be manipulated into running away with Delia, Evan, Sebastian, and Ashling. Delia did not kill her, but helped fake her suicide so that they could all be on the run again forever. Delia needed June because of her dark obsession, Evan wanted her to go with them because of her witnessing the murder and knowing too much about everyone's situations and identities, Ashling was jealous of June and really didn't want her to be there but loved Delia too much to say so, and Sebastian I think was the only one who truly cared about June and genuinely felt regret that she was forced into this life with them<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1296842529" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1296842529" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1296842529?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781405271578" href="/book/show/24991736-suicide-notes-from-beautiful-girls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1296842529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18187328063819270923"><i>
  <b>Delia knew something someone didn’t want her to know, that’s for damn sure. And she threatened to tell. So whose secret was it? And what were they willing to do to make her keep it?</b>
</i><br/><br/>Lovely cover, intriguing title, nothing new or special for the most part, until a cheap twist comes flying in towards the end.<br/><br/>This book was all kinds of messy. Typical bitchy high-school drama that tries to follow in the footsteps of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21480930.Gone_Girl' title='Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gone Girl</a>, but ends up being laughably cheesy, rather than an interesting psychol</span>
  <span id="freeText18187328063819270923" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>Delia knew something someone didn’t want her to know, that’s for damn sure. And she threatened to tell. So whose secret was it? And what were they willing to do to make her keep it?</b>
</i><br /><br />Lovely cover, intriguing title, nothing new or special for the most part, until a cheap twist comes flying in towards the end.<br /><br />This book was all kinds of messy. Typical bitchy high-school drama that tries to follow in the footsteps of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21480930.Gone_Girl" title="Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Gone Girl</a>, but ends up being laughably cheesy, rather than an interesting psychological thriller. Plus, it seems like a mistake to market this as "Gone Girl meets Thirteen Reasons Why" when that makes it really easy to see the "twist" coming.<br /><br />I've read multiple variations of the "girl commits suicide but - oh my - it might not really be a suicide and now the best friend must solve this murder case without consulting the police" story. Do they ever work? Not that I can remember. Mostly because I have little patience for stupid people and there's something inherently stupid about finding evidence that someone might have been murdered and launching your own investigation.<br /><br />This one, however, is particularly sensational. June and Delia used to be friends but "something happened". June gets a voice mail from Delia the day of her alleged suicide, and then Delia's ex-boyfriend turns up and announces that she didn't kill herself. So June throws herself into a private investigation that gets more and more unbelievable as it progresses.<br /><br />The plot goes a little crazy - from drugs to cheating to pregnancy to abortion to rape - and June's characterization is a little off. Her first discovery is that *gasp* Delia is involved with a drug dealer. June's initial reaction implies that she is terrified and clueless at the thought of drugs (I mean, like, marijuana's that herb they put in tacos, right?) Then, all of a sudden, she's infiltrating the drug dealer's lair (okay, going to his house, but remember - this is a dramatic book).<br /><br />Some people were surprised by the ending, but I think so much gives it away. There's too many clues in the marketing, for a start. And not only is it easy to guess, but I think it weakens the story even further. Delia's somewhat complex character dissolves into just one more cliche.<br /><br />Disappointing.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="18187328063819270923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

June trusted Jeremiah too fast. Like he could be the f</span>
  <span id="freeText14450435458619791076" style="display:none">This is probably going to be a difficult review to write, but<br><br>Let's start.<br><br><b>First of all, the MC, June is the stupidest, retarded piece of shit on Earth.</b> Her "best friend" (who she stopped talking to) Delia commit suicide, but smart-ass June thinks she was murdered! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476924903ra/20897624.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Okay that's fine, but June <b>kept on</b> going back and forth between either she was murdered or she commit suicide. <b>Girl, make up your fucking mind please.</b> <br><br>-She trusted people to easily. June trusted Jeremiah too fast. Like he could be the fucking murderer for all you know, but your still going to follow his pretty little ass looking for clues. <br><br>-She legit went into the 'murderer's home' and was hoping he wouldn't kill her. (She is fucking stupid right?)<br>She also goes up to people asking for the murderer's evil lair. Okay bitch you just want to get killed don't you? WHY ARE YOU SO FUCKING STUPID?<br><br>June has like no fucking emotion. Your best friend died. Can you at least <b>try</b> to be fucking sad?? I don't even think she cried. Like this brings me to the writing. Did a twelve or thirteen year old write this? I don't believe an adult wrote this. There is no emotion put into the writing. The fucking characters sound <b>dead</b> themselves. June and the other dude just plainly say "we're going to solve this murder" like it's the most natural fucking thing in the world.<br><br><b>The plot:</b><br>There was a fucking plot?<br>Why didn't anyone tell me there was a solid, legit plot in this book?<br>WHAT PLOT???<br><br>What the fuck was the author smoking when she wrote this? Like she seems to be writing one thing and all of a sudden BOOM some other shit happens and the first part of the story never even happened. <br><br>Like the first part of the story talks about how June is going to solve Delia's murder(?) (how can you even be so sure it was murder?), but in the second part (which is after like a 100 pages or so) there's a huge plot twist and the first part of the book <b>doesn't even matter.</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Like what the fuck was with that supernatural shit? Did Delia come back from the fucking dead?? Or was June just really fucking high?? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Also the ending has left me confused and has leaved me with some unanswered questions. <br><br><b>The plot twist:</b><br>Again, I was not surprised. Meh.<br><br>Overall, this was <b>not</b> a thriller. It was shit. <br><br><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1461874250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13624591380068198190">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Pitched as Gone Girl meets Thirteen Reasons Why”</i>
</b><br/><br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449677430ra/17323427.gif' alt='Palm Springs commercial photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><i>Suicide Notes From Beautiful Girls</i> was one of the pop-up recommendations on my library homepage. I had heard zilch about this book before requesting it and only did so because I liked the title. (Deep, I know.) Then I saw that sales pitch contained in the blurb and had the following reaction . . . <br/><br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449677430ra/17323428.gif' alt='Palm Springs commercial photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>However, since I have no ability to <b>not</b> read a book once it is downloaded, I ha</span>
  <span id="freeText13624591380068198190" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br><b>
  <i>“Pitched as Gone Girl meets Thirteen Reasons Why”</i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449677430ra/17323427.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>Suicide Notes From Beautiful Girls</i> was one of the pop-up recommendations on my library homepage. I had heard zilch about this book before requesting it and only did so because I liked the title. (Deep, I know.) Then I saw that sales pitch contained in the blurb and had the following reaction . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449677430ra/17323428.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>However, since I have no ability to <b>not</b> read a book once it is downloaded, I had no choice but to grin and bear it. And you know what? This was kinda like <i>Gone Girl</i>. Now if I were Jay Asher I’d probably want to kick someone’s ass for trivializing my suicide book (as contrived as I found it to be), but if you’re looking for YA with some mindf*&amp;^ery this one might be a winner. <br><br><b>
  <i> “Having secrets together makes you real friends. Secrets tie you together.”</i>
</b><br><br>Delia had plenty of secrets. Secrets about her boyfriend and her stepfather and her best friend June and maybe even June’s boyfriend. But all of those secrets died along with Delia . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449677430ra/17323429.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Or did they?<br><br>June and Delia had drifted apart, as friends sometimes do. When June hears that Delia committed suicide she feels guilty for not answering Delia’s call. Guilt soon morphs into suspicion when she listens to the voice mail left by Delia right before her death and after she meets Delia’s ex-boyfriend. Did Delia really kill herself or was she murdered?<br><br>I was a little concerned when I guessed a potential major plot point at the 5% mark and then had it confirmed by 20% . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449677430ra/17323430.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I also figured <i>something</i> more than that had to be up because there was too much book left and since I had read . . . . some another book (not <i>Gone Girl</i>) which shall remain nameless in order to avoid spoilage . . . . it was pretty easy to figure out the second twist in the story as well. Buuuuuuuuut, even though I saw <b>most</b> of the things coming, I didn’t see them all . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449677430ra/17323431.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>and I never wanted to stop turning pages. I would obviously ruin the fun if I told <i>anything</i> about the twists and turns the story took. All I’ll say is (a) I read <b>a poopton</b> of mystery/thrillers so when it comes to guessing what’s going to happen next I’m fairly good at it and (b) a lot can be forgiven if the author sticks the <s>landing</s> ending. I seriously dug the end of this one.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Sometimes the kindest thing you can do for a person is to shield them from that which will not help them. Make the decision and then carry the burden yourself, bear that weight so that they don’t have to.”</i>
</b><br></span>

<div id="review_1309067249" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1309067249" />
    <a title="Stacee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7359586-stacee"><img alt="Stacee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577910954p2/7359586.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1309067249?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacee" href="/user/show/7359586-stacee">Stacee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7359586-stacee?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7359586-stacee?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1309067249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8706133038378921178">1.5 stars?<br/><br/>First off, I am 100% on board with mindfuckery. I love it. Like an all caps, flailing sort of love. This...this was disappointing. <br/><br/>Well, the first 40% of the book was good. I was definitely intrigued at the murder/mystery/conspiracy vibe I was getting. Then there was a maybe cheating boyfriend/maybe shitty BFF plot line and I sort of lost my taste for it. <br/><br/>When the truth came out, it was enough to keep me going; however, I loathe not getting concrete answers when mindfuckery is a major </span>
  <span id="freeText8706133038378921178" style="display:none">1.5 stars?<br /><br />First off, I am 100% on board with mindfuckery. I love it. Like an all caps, flailing sort of love. This...this was disappointing. <br /><br />Well, the first 40% of the book was good. I was definitely intrigued at the murder/mystery/conspiracy vibe I was getting. Then there was a maybe cheating boyfriend/maybe shitty BFF plot line and I sort of lost my taste for it. <br /><br />When the truth came out, it was enough to keep me going; however, I loathe not getting concrete answers when mindfuckery is a major theme. I got to the end of the story and still wasn't sure exactly what happened. The switch between present day 1st person and past tense 3rd person was jarring and kept me from getting into the rhythm of the story. <br /><br />June and Delia are odd together as friends. Their friendship seems toxic, not supportive. There are a few other characters that had potential, but were never given dimension. <br /><br />Overall, it was a captivating premise with an execution that fell flat. I know a lot of people will enjoy this, but it just wasn't for me. <br /><br />**Huge thanks to Simon Pulse and Edelweiss for providing the arc in exchange for an honest review**</span>
  <a data-text-id="8706133038378921178" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1249608348" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1249608348" />
    <a title="Es Summer " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15104379-es-summer"><img alt="Es Summer " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466450844p2/15104379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1249608348?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Es Summer " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Es Summer " href="/user/show/15104379-es-summer">Es Summer </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15104379-es-summer?shelf=favorites-2015">favorites-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15104379-es-summer?shelf=favorite-books-forever">favorite-books-forever</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1249608348" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11473260133323702067"><br/><b>
  <i> "Our hearts are pounding,<br/>And I can't tell whose is whose,<br/>her palms on my face,<br/>her lips on mine,<br/>her heart inside my chest." </i>
</b><br/><br/>Lately I've been craving this new type of books. Books about women and their relationship with each other. Books about the intense, sometimes twisted and hypnotizing friendship women have with each other. I love the way girls love each other recklessly and wild. <br/>Unconstrained and passionately. <br/><br/>Suicide Notes from Beautiful Girls is about a consuming, intense friendship b</span>
  <span id="freeText11473260133323702067" style="display:none"><br /><b>
  <i> "Our hearts are pounding,<br />And I can't tell whose is whose,<br />her palms on my face,<br />her lips on mine,<br />her heart inside my chest." </i>
</b><br /><br />Lately I've been craving this new type of books. Books about women and their relationship with each other. Books about the intense, sometimes twisted and hypnotizing friendship women have with each other. I love the way girls love each other recklessly and wild. <br />Unconstrained and passionately. <br /><br />Suicide Notes from Beautiful Girls is about a consuming, intense friendship between two girls gone wrong.<br />June's former best friend, Delia, commits suicide and leaves June confused and sad. Something about the suicide of her former best friend doesn't sit her right and she starts to search for the truth. <br /><br /><b>
  <i> "Delia would explain to June that finding a best friend is like finding a true love: when you meet yours, you just know." </i>
</b><br /><br />Melancholic.<br />That's the feeling I got from reading the book. Suicide Notes from Beautiful Girls has something hypnotizing about it. The toxic friendship between these girls had me in its power.<br /><br />The characters are interesting and multi-layered. Delia is an enigma, an untamed girl who makes bad choices. Through the flash backs you get the know her better and I caught myself wanting to connect with her. <br />Let's be honest: a slightly crazy person with not entirely good intentions makes a more interesting story than a 'nice' person.<br />I'm always fascinated when I read books about crazy minds.<br />Delia is selfish, slightly insane, but I liked her. I loved the way she was described. The way you got little glimpses of her softer side.<br /><br />The ending is very unexpected and leaves you wanting more!<br />Overall: a great psychological thriller about girls and their relationship with each other. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11473260133323702067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781481418539" href="/book/show/23309655-suicide-notes-from-beautiful-girls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16069171-aditi?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16069171-aditi?shelf=friends">friends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16069171-aditi?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16069171-aditi?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16069171-aditi?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16069171-aditi?shelf=my-reviews">my-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16069171-aditi?shelf=simon-schuster-books">simon-schuster-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1328805767" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10256337814829380911"> <i>“However rare true love may be, it is less so than true friendship.” </i><br/><br/> ----Albert Einstein<br/><br/>Lynn Weingarten, an American YA author, pens a gripping as well as an emotional tale, <i>Suicide Notes from Beautiful Girls </i>, about two friends layered with enough mystery to keep the readers engaged till the very end, in a way, the author shades light into teenage friendships, trust issues among them, teenage trauma and suicide and mysterious death into her plot.<br/><br/><br/><b>Synopsis: </b><br/><br/><i>Gone Girl meets 13 Reasons Why in thi</i></span>
  <span id="freeText10256337814829380911" style="display:none"> <i>“However rare true love may be, it is less so than true friendship.” </i><br /><br /> ----Albert Einstein<br /><br />Lynn Weingarten, an American YA author, pens a gripping as well as an emotional tale, <i>Suicide Notes from Beautiful Girls </i>, about two friends layered with enough mystery to keep the readers engaged till the very end, in a way, the author shades light into teenage friendships, trust issues among them, teenage trauma and suicide and mysterious death into her plot.<br /><br /><br /><b>Synopsis: </b><br /><br /><i>Gone Girl meets 13 Reasons Why in this stylish, sexy, and atmospheric story about friendship packed with twists and turns that will leave you breathless.<br /><br />They say Delia burned herself to death in her stepfather's shed. They say it was suicide.<br /><br />But June doesn't believe it.<br /><br />June and Delia used to be closer than anything. Best friends in that way that comes before everyone else-before guys, before family. It was like being in love, but more. They had a billion secrets, tying them together like thin silk cords.<br /><br />But one night a year ago, everything changed. June, Delia, and June's boyfriend Ryan were just having a little fun. Their good time got out of hand. And in the cold blue light of morning, June knew only this-things would never be the same again.<br /><br />And now, a year later, Delia is dead. June is certain she was murdered. And she owes it to her to find out the truth...which is far more complicated than she ever could have imagined. </i><br /><br /><br />Delia and June, two high school teenagers were best friends forever and their bond was stronger than blood, but that was a year ago, when everything was perfect between them, June existing in her emotional and caring shell with her boyfriend, Ryan, whereas Delia leading her wild, vulnerable and rough life with drugs, lovers, etc. But due to a stroke of bad luck, things become so weak and mistrusting between June and Delia which took them to a point when they never talked to one another anymore. One year later, when Delia's death of burning herself to death, is announced on the PA system and when on Delia's memorial service, Delia's then boyfriend claimed that it was not a suicide rather it was a murder, it leads June to start an investigation to find out the reasons behind Delia's possible murder. Or it was very possible that June's own judgement and emotions were deluding her mind from accepting Delia's death as a suicide.<br /><br /><br />The writing style is okay not that good in fact. The narrative is also fine and sometimes it is engaging enough to keep the readers hooked on to the story. The prose is articulate with enough twists and turns to keep the readers on their toes. The pacing is steady and there goes the flaw which made the story not a memorable one- the plot which kept on going up and down and there never is a steady moment to make the readers sway with the story-telling.<br /><br />The plot is quite inconsistent, with the first half of the mystery being quite simple and nothing so unraveling, while the second half being filled with lots of twists and turns that confuses the readers a lot. Moreover, the climax did not suit the story, at least that's what I feel about it, I mean climax can be shown in a complicated manner but the character that the author incorporated into the minds of the readers while narrating the story lose it's charm in the end. <br /><br />The characterization is not that strong, with June being the main character, who is very naive and an emotional wreck, but at times, she acted brave and so coolly among things which scared her, although there is no consistent transformation in June's character to comprehend with her sudden change of demeanor. Other than that, she is caring and determined teenager to get to the bottom of the truth.<br /><br />Delia is a dark character and surprisingly her flaws made her look so perfect through the pages of the book. Yes, although her much-hyped death shies like a true-crime thriller, but there is so much confusion among the characters that at times, this confusion and teasing with the twists fail to excite the readers. Not a single character is portrayed with depth, thus leaving the readers minds with lots of unanswered questions behind the dark secrets that everyone seems to with-hold among themselves.<br /><br />The mystery is good, and nicely depicted and keeps the readers on their edges till the very climax. There is bit of chemistry and lots of dark elements and the story revolves between the past and the present, where the present is narrated in first person POV with the past being narrated in the third person POV, and the way they swayed from one time period to another is strikingly done by the author. So that makes the readers to fall into the "keep-on-guessing-mode" till the entire length of the novel. And yeah it is a bit of a <i>Gone Girl</i> type story.<br /><br /><b>Verdict: </b> <i>I wouldn't recommend it too strongly but if you enjoy a nice thriller based on friendships, then this book perfectly fits the bill. </i><br /><br /><b>Courtesy: </b> <i>Thanks to the author's publishers for giving me an opportunity to read and review the book. </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10256337814829380911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7798382781662819292">I have just finished this novel and all I can say is what the holy heck? The whole thing was addictively brilliant but THAT ENDING OH MY! I am not entirely sure what I'm feeling right now but that was powerful powerful stuff.<br/><br/>June's best friend has committed suicide. They had drifted apart in the months leading up to the tragedy and June is struggling with survivor guilt. However things are strange - and lead her to believe that perhaps this is not as straightforward as it seems. Did Delia really</span>
  <span id="freeText7798382781662819292" style="display:none">I have just finished this novel and all I can say is what the holy heck? The whole thing was addictively brilliant but THAT ENDING OH MY! I am not entirely sure what I'm feeling right now but that was powerful powerful stuff.<br /><br />June's best friend has committed suicide. They had drifted apart in the months leading up to the tragedy and June is struggling with survivor guilt. However things are strange - and lead her to believe that perhaps this is not as straightforward as it seems. Did Delia really kill herself? Or did someone help her along the way...<br /><br />Ok so basically what you have here is a brilliantly complex but eminently readable mystery story, with a central character at the heart of it who is enigmatic, superbly drawn, difficult to get a handle on and so deeply fascinating that I will never forget her. Secondly you have a beautifully written and emotionally resonant story of one girl and her search for the truth.<br /><br />This book WILL mess with your head, in the best way, as the twists and turns and "oh my gosh" moments come thick and fast - but never ever does the author allow this to detract from the character driven heart of this story which is one of deep seated friendships and the things that both drive us apart and keep us together. It is a tale of psychological depth which is also a heart stopping thrill ride of the highest order.<br /><br />About 3/4 of the way through my head was almost exploding as June gets shock after shock, Lynn Weingarten puts the pressure on in a gorgeously written style that hits you BAM, right in the guts. I had no idea where this was going ultimately, as we headed into THAT finish, I was agog, I could not turn the pages fast enough. <br /><br />A powerhouse of a novel that will leave you speechless. <br /><br />Highly Recommended<br /><br />Happy Reading Folks! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14849402924898459866"><b>1 star </b> for plot itself and being well written.<br/><b>1 star</b> for it being engrossing and keeping my attention.<br/><b>1 star </b> for overall not feeling like it was a total waste of my time.<br/><br/><u>
  <b>trigger warnings!!! suicide, rape, and addiction. </b>
</u><br/>Also, it has HEAVY language. Just an FYI for those of you who may not like that.<br/><br/>I'll just start off by stating that I think that the book had a quite promising plot.<br/>The idea of the book was very intriguing, but in the end, the book fell short of my<br/>expectations. <br/><br/>Character De</span>
  <span id="freeText14849402924898459866" style="display:none"><b>1 star </b> for plot itself and being well written.<br /><b>1 star</b> for it being engrossing and keeping my attention.<br /><b>1 star </b> for overall not feeling like it was a total waste of my time.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>trigger warnings!!! suicide, rape, and addiction. </b>
</u><br />Also, it has HEAVY language. Just an FYI for those of you who may not like that.<br /><br />I'll just start off by stating that I think that the book had a quite promising plot.<br />The idea of the book was very intriguing, but in the end, the book fell short of my<br />expectations. <br /><br />Character Developement wasn't horrible, but i found every character in this book to be extremely unlikeable.<br /><br />The story follows two friends who had a falling out, one of them supposedly commits suicide and the other begins to investigate said suicide with doubts. June doesn't believe her friend Delia, who was terrified of fire, committed suicide by burning herself alive, so she begins to look further into the suicide and things soon begin to reveal themselves to her.<br /><br />This book was very engrossing, i never had to "force" myself to pick it up. However, it was very predictable and I knew who not to trust from the very first page...no matter how "promising" the book tried to portray them as.<br /><br />I found June to be too gullible and annoying. I found Delia to be extremely dark and creepy.<br />Ryan was just blah, as was every other supportive character in this book.<br /><br />Also, I still don't quite understand the relationship between the two main characters. It was just weird.<br /><br />The ending disappointed me and frankly, pissed me off. My mood was ruined the minute I finished the last paragraph. <br /><br />Overall, it wasn't terrible... however it did mess me up a little inside and now I'm unsure if I ever want to read another book by this author or not.<br /><br />Ughhhh, I'm going to go lull this book over in my brain for awhile.</span>

    <div class="updateActionLinks">

<div id="review_1315403496" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1315403496" />
    <a title="Nicola" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8803703-nicola"><img alt="Nicola" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587222161p2/8803703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1315403496?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicola" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicola" href="/user/show/8803703-nicola">Nicola</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781405271578" href="/book/show/24991736-suicide-notes-from-beautiful-girls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8803703-nicola?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1315403496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer410393873337999997">I have mixed feelings about <i>Suicide Notes from Beautiful Girls</i>. On the one hand it's an exciting thriller that kept me on the edge of my seat. On the other hand, in the last 50% the book becomes weird and insane and it was like a whole different book.<br/><br/>June and Delia are former best friends and haven't spoken in over a year because of "something" that happened. June receives a voicemail on the day that Delia supposedly kills herself but then Delia's boyfriend arrives and says he doesn't believe it</span>
  <span id="freeText410393873337999997" style="display:none">I have mixed feelings about <i>Suicide Notes from Beautiful Girls</i>. On the one hand it's an exciting thriller that kept me on the edge of my seat. On the other hand, in the last 50% the book becomes weird and insane and it was like a whole different book.<br /><br />June and Delia are former best friends and haven't spoken in over a year because of "something" that happened. June receives a voicemail on the day that Delia supposedly kills herself but then Delia's boyfriend arrives and says he doesn't believe it. June feels guilty that she didn't answer her phone and so launches her own investigation into what really happened because the police aren't willing to help.<br /><br />The characters are one of the impressive areas of the book. There are complexities in their lives that makes them more interesting to read about. We are introduced to a new set of characters in the second half of the book who I found to also be intriguing. There are flashbacks throughout the book so that we can learn more of Delia and June's friendship before they drifted apart and this was a useful way to get to know a character who is dead.<br /><br />I really enjoyed this initial mystery of what actually happened to Delia. Did she really kill herself? Or was it someone in the bad crowd she was involved with? I liked that there were various conspiracies and suspects and that it could have been any one of them. Then things get insane half way through when the twist happens. I think it's a bit of a faux pas for the marketing to compare the book to Gone Girl. I can't say too much without spoiling the twist but I saw it coming.<br /><br />The ending is very abrupt and it's one of those endings that you have to figure out for yourself. Things aren't completely resolved or explained and so you have to make your own conclusions. Maybe it makes me a lazy reader but in this type of book (one full of many twists and turns) I like to have some proper answers at the end. The ending is so abrupt that I'm not even really sure what actually happened.<br /><br />I still mostly enjoyed this book as I love thrillers and conspiracies and this really did keep me on the edge of my seat. I read it in one day. The ending is just a little disappointing.<br /><br /><i>I received a copy of this book from the publisher via Netgalley.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="410393873337999997" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Sue" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7377874-sue"><img alt="Sue" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594207220p2/7377874.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1382352235?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue" href="/user/show/7377874-sue">Sue</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1382352235" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4916021636376575021"><br/><br/>Although this is classified as YA, I personally think anyone can read this. I am middle aged and I <b>loved </b> this book. Its definitely a WOW what happened there....<br/><br/><br/>This is jam packed with an emotional read, two friends, Delia and June. Both are so very different in character. Whilst Delia comes across wild and out of control at times, June comes across as more mild. I think Delia brings confidence to June, until......<br/><br/>Delia leaves a suicide note.<br/><br/>This is where action starts to happen. June knows the </span>
  <span id="freeText4916021636376575021" style="display:none"><br /><br />Although this is classified as YA, I personally think anyone can read this. I am middle aged and I <b>loved </b> this book. Its definitely a WOW what happened there....<br /><br /><br />This is jam packed with an emotional read, two friends, Delia and June. Both are so very different in character. Whilst Delia comes across wild and out of control at times, June comes across as more mild. I think Delia brings confidence to June, until......<br /><br />Delia leaves a suicide note.<br /><br />This is where action starts to happen. June knows the fear Delia has of a fire so, why would she commit suicide where fire is involved? It doesn't add up.<br /><br />Then, she gets to know that Delia's boyfriend feels she was killed and not that Delia took her own life.<br /><br />The hunt is on..<br /><br />I feel so differently about this story compared to some reviews I have read, I liked this book, I liked it a lot. It kept me thinking, it kept my attention and I thought the author did a fantastic job with the plot. <br /><br />It didn't appear messy or confusing, I followed it very well and the ending was a surprise to me that I didn't expect, which is another plus for me.<br /><br />I would certainly read more from this author and say, read this for yourself, because I thoroughly enjoyed the writing and the plot.<br /><br />**Thank you to Egmont Publishing via Net Galley for my copy**<br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2096219974" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15200263390569012330"><b>1 star</b><br/><br/>This book was just so messed up. Like, probably the most messed up book I've ever read.<br/><br/>In a mere 300 pages, it goes from the basic high school party life messed up to straight up murdering people messed up. Every time I thought it couldn't get worse, I was wrong. The main character is lied to so many times by the end of the book it's hard for even the reader to keep everything straight. It honestly took me a little while to sort everything out.<br/><br/>The worst thing about this book is that there </span>
  <span id="freeText15200263390569012330" style="display:none"><b>1 star</b><br /><br />This book was just so messed up. Like, probably the most messed up book I've ever read.<br /><br />In a mere 300 pages, it goes from the basic high school party life messed up to straight up murdering people messed up. Every time I thought it couldn't get worse, I was wrong. The main character is lied to so many times by the end of the book it's hard for even the reader to keep everything straight. It honestly took me a little while to sort everything out.<br /><br />The worst thing about this book is that there is no resolution. It just keeps going downhill. And keeps going. And going. And the ending? It's the worst of all.<br /><br />The largest problem lies within the other main character, Delia. She's so manipulative and wild that she doesn't just drag herself down to the pits of hell (I'm not even kidding this is the only way to describe it), she also drags everyone else with her. Especially those who mean well. And not only that, she claims to do it out of love. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Threatening to kill yourself if your "loved" one doesn't go along with murder and then fake her death is not love. No excuses. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Really, I honestly can't believe that some people can read this book and not think, "this is not okay in the slightest." </span>

  <span id="freeText2138554178192191585" style="display:none">Contains so many of my favorite elements, including a toxic homoerotic friendship and some good old-fashioned revenge questing, as well as some really lovely writing.   <span id="freeText14793307733282041762" style="display:none">Trigger Warnings: <u> Suicide and Rape </u> <br><br>One word to describe this would be <b> Disappointing. </b> <br><br>This has a solid premise for a young adult book involving suicide. Someone's best friend supposedly kills herself, through burning herself. But her friend June is shocked by her death and believes it to be not her doing. <br><br>June was an okay character and for the most part I liked her, than the book went down hill and so did her character for me. Her "best friend" Delia is <u> obnoxious! </u> Not only is she a character full of tropes but her lines are usually offensive and concerning. She does a great job at portraying unhealthy relationships with everyone she meets. <br><br> <p> Just this is a quote from Delia involving abortion, <br><b> <i> "I sure as hell would kill that baby though" </i> </b> <br>Which her buddy responds with, <br><b> <i> "It wouldn't be a baby yet... I mean not at first... It would be goo" </i> </b> </p> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456563263ra/18249308.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Those quotes basically explain the girls relationship. They truthfully brings out the absolute <i> worst </i> in one another. Not only does Delia drag June along like a puppy but gets her in serious trouble. <br><br><p> <b> <i> "Junnie opens and closes her sweet mouth like a fish. I want to shove my fingers in there, to stick therm all the way down her throat until I reach her heart" </i> </b> </p> <br><br><s> Like is she okayyy???????? </s> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423543222ra/13641439.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Not only was this a disappointment, the first quarter was decent. I mean I read this in a day! But this went in a direction that was just not good. Like this book is full of bad relationships, drugs and smoking, and sex. With trying to be a dark book talking about suicide, it was not that. <br><br></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=a-jack-in-the-box-pop-surprise">a-jack-in-the-box-pop-surprise</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=cheap-thrills-but-i-loved-it">cheap-thrills-but-i-loved-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=pulp-junk-i-adore">pulp-junk-i-adore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=bizarre-wtf">bizarre-wtf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=black-gleeful-fun">black-gleeful-fun</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=older-teen">older-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=awesomely-horrifying-loved-it">awesomely-horrifying-loved-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=best-if-read-cold">best-if-read-cold</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3409532-april-does-feral-sometimes?shelf=mysteries-potboilers-thrillers">mysteries-potboilers-thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3515088693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14356200033992775870">‘Suicide Notes From Beautiful Girls’ by Lynn Weingarten is a taut thriller about a Svengali teen relationship. The plot is not beyond belief to me because, <i>*blush*,</i> I read a lot of news media and I watch movies besides spending my time reading books. I know there have been a few girl friendships in real life where affection and teen friendship spun up into madness.<br/><br/>In some ways, the novel reminded me of the movie ‘Heavenly Creatures’ which is based on a true story. <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://youtu.be/kJ2yZjnPwQc'>https://youtu.be/kJ2yZjnPwQc</a> an</span>
  <span id="freeText14356200033992775870" style="display:none">‘Suicide Notes From Beautiful Girls’ by Lynn Weingarten is a taut thriller about a Svengali teen relationship. The plot is not beyond belief to me because, <i>*blush*,</i> I read a lot of news media and I watch movies besides spending my time reading books. I know there have been a few girl friendships in real life where affection and teen friendship spun up into madness.<br /><br />In some ways, the novel reminded me of the movie ‘Heavenly Creatures’ which is based on a true story. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/kJ2yZjnPwQc">https://youtu.be/kJ2yZjnPwQc</a> and <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heavenly_Creatures">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heavenl...</a><br /><br />There also was the true crime story of two twelve-year-old girls who tried to kill one of their best friends in a bizarre ritual : <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slender_Man_stabbing">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slender...</a><br /><br /><br />Now that I probably have you interested to some degree, I feel reluctant to write of the plot of ‘Suicide Notes From Beautiful Girls’ in too much detail. But I’ll spill it a little. <br /><br />I recognized that the main narrator, June, was in a Svengali relationship with her best friend Delia after a few chapters, although that fact is not explicitly mentioned at all. I could tell Delia was the Svengali, and maybe a psychopath. <br /><br />The two girls met in the sixth grade and they each immediately felt the other was their soul mate. Some of Delia’s past, revealed in flashbacks strategically remembered by June, show that Delia has been an outlaw kid who colors outside the lines for a long time. She uses people when there is an opportunity to do so as if they were chess pieces to amuse herself since she was only eleven years old. She seems fearless. Her mother remarried, and Delia despises her stepfather, a university professor. She hears him abuse her mother. She despises her mother for being weak-willed. However, she doesn’t have a master plan or goals until an incident occurs when she is a junior in high school. <br /><br />June, Delia’s best friend, is oblivious of how far Delia can go when she has reason to do so. June is a follower. Everything Delia does beguiles and enchants June. June is an innocent despite her alcoholic mother and her occasionally scary life at home. June is conventional and kind without much insight into Evil or darker motives.<br /><br />Both girls share feelings of depression, and of not fitting in. June is afraid of anyone finding out about her mother’s alcoholism - except for Delia. She can tell Delia anything! June spends many comfortable years going over to Delia’s house after school. They are inseparable - until Ryan asks June out for a date. June is thrilled! Delia has boyfriends too, like Jeremiah, but she does not seem as thrilled with them as June is with Ryan. Then Delia makes a play for Ryan. June cannot forgive her friend. She stops seeing Delia.<br /><br />Then in home room, it’s announced Delia is dead from a horrible fire! Delia had left a voice message before the fire on June’s cell which she had not bothered to answer. What could have happened! Everyone believes it was suicide. That cannot be! Delia hated fires!<br /><br />There is a puzzle here. June begins to ask around the high school if the kids knew what Delia had been doing, who were her friends, what parties had she attended. June needs to know what happened to her best friend!<br /><br />I have noticed many on Goodreads who have read this YA thriller are disappointed in the novel. Some think it too unrealistic - they don’t believe in what I know is a Svengali relationship can actually exist. I suspect they never heard of that. Others hate the ending because it is a trick ending. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I think Delia lied about her stepfather trying to rape her, but I believe she was extremely angry that her stepfather beat up on her mother. As a psychopath, Delia would have easily seen that in meeting the other three criminals, which is not explained by the author but I suspect was through meeting Ashling at a party by Tig, the drug dealer, was an opportunity to do something about her boring life and her stepfather. I think June wrote the suicide note at the end and left town with Delia and her friends. June was in too deep. Although June was terrified of their murderous criminality and cruelty, I think that a follower-type character would have crumpled under the strength of Delia’s will whatever her horror, plus she WAS guilty as an accessory. However, I wouldn’t place any bets on how long she would stay with the gang. June might run like a rabbit at some low emotional point because of guilt. Delia certainly could give the order to kill June if June was a threat to the gang’s safety. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The book has its faults, but I think it was a very satisfying YA <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19288043.Gone_Girl" title="Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Gone Girl</a> clone except for that full-stop mysterious ending! It put the brakes on too suddenly! It wasn’t simply too baffling. It was too bewildering.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14356200033992775870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1230815409" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1230815409" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31923026-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533734143p2/31923026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1230815409?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/31923026-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=e-arc">e-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=crime-mystery-thriller">crime-mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1230815409" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14426987963854836920">2.5 stars<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18244970.Suicide_Notes_from_Beautiful_Girls' title='Suicide Notes from Beautiful Girls by Lynn Weingarten' rel='nofollow noopener'> Suicide Notes From Beautiful Girls</a> sets out to do what <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21480930.Gone_Girl' title='Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn' rel='nofollow noopener'> Gone Girl</a> once did and shock us all, but falls short of that while still managing some entertainment throughout.<br/><br/>The problem is more that too much is given away for that shock and awe to happen. It doesn’t exactly help that in the book’s description is “pitched as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21480930.Gone_Girl' title='Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn' rel='nofollow noopener'> Gone Girl</a> meets <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1217100.Thirteen_Reasons_Why' title='Thirteen Reasons Why by Jay Asher' rel='nofollow noopener'> Thirteen Reasons Why</a>.” The twists are given away right there, so with these books in mind, the reader can anticipate what happens. This aside - the stor</span>
  <span id="freeText14426987963854836920" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18244970.Suicide_Notes_from_Beautiful_Girls" title="Suicide Notes from Beautiful Girls by Lynn Weingarten" rel="nofollow noopener"> Suicide Notes From Beautiful Girls</a> sets out to do what <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21480930.Gone_Girl" title="Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener"> Gone Girl</a> once did and shock us all, but falls short of that while still managing some entertainment throughout.<br /><br />The problem is more that too much is given away for that shock and awe to happen. It doesn’t exactly help that in the book’s description is “pitched as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21480930.Gone_Girl" title="Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener"> Gone Girl</a> meets <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1217100.Thirteen_Reasons_Why" title="Thirteen Reasons Why by Jay Asher" rel="nofollow noopener"> Thirteen Reasons Why</a>.” The twists are given away right there, so with these books in mind, the reader can anticipate what happens. This aside - the story was still entertaining and succeeded in giving thrills at times.<br /><br />This book is about a girl named June who learns that her former best friend committed suicide. The two haven’t spoken in a year, but June can’t help but wonder why Delia, her old friend, would do this. It doesn’t help that June ignored a call from Delia the day before she died. If June had picked up, would her former friend still be here? Why exactly did Delia try to call June anyway? Is there something more to Delia’s death than anyone realizes? June starts looking at her friend’s death as a murder and begins her own investigation of sorts. The story is full of flashbacks to Delia and June’s friendship and eventually fills us in as to why the two stopped being friends in the first place. We are also slowly enlightened as to what exactly happened to Delia. There are twists that are supposed to be shocking, but for the reasons I stated earlier that did not happen for me. Also, I wish there was a bit more to the explanation in the very end. I really enjoyed Delia in the book and wish there was a bit more on her character, as well.<br /><br />Overall, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18244970.Suicide_Notes_from_Beautiful_Girls" title="Suicide Notes from Beautiful Girls by Lynn Weingarten" rel="nofollow noopener"> Suicide Notes From Beautiful Girls</a> is a very intriguing concept that if described differently in the synopsis, could have felt better executed. I would still recommend this book to anyone looking for a mystery thriller in the young adult genre. This one wasn’t my favorite, but it is still enjoyable.<br /><br /><br /><b>I received an ARC in exchange for an honest review via edelweiss.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14426987963854836920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1666827882" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1666827882" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1666827882?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2016">z-read2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1666827882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3363192041110852346">3.5 stars. Cheesy in places and not particularly new, but definitely an enjoyable, psychological read. <br/><br/><b>TO START WITH: THE BAD</b> <br/><br/><b>It's cliche.</b> I think we've all read plenty of books with slightly naive leads and evil opposite characters. Anyone who's read YA suspense of this type will know the approximate direction the plot is headed. This didn't affect my enjoyment of the book, especially since I read this before becoming tired of the cliche, but YA suspense veterans, be warned. <br/><br/>Another complaint: </span>
  <span id="freeText3363192041110852346" style="display:none">3.5 stars. Cheesy in places and not particularly new, but definitely an enjoyable, psychological read. <br /><br /><b>TO START WITH: THE BAD</b> <br /><br /><b>It's cliche.</b> I think we've all read plenty of books with slightly naive leads and evil opposite characters. Anyone who's read YA suspense of this type will know the approximate direction the plot is headed. This didn't affect my enjoyment of the book, especially since I read this before becoming tired of the cliche, but YA suspense veterans, be warned. <br /><br />Another complaint: June's character has moments of development and interest, but she comes across a little too <b>naive</b> for my taste. She develops out of this to some degree, but not to my satisfaction, sadly. <br /><br /><b>AND NOW: THE GOOD</b><br /><br />While June was a little annoying, the complexity of Delia's character definitely stands out here. She's an interesting, morally ambiguous character - not all black or all white. In fact, many readers will view her in different ways. <br /><br />The pacing is a little off, but in a way, it actually contributes to the <b>atmosphere </b> of the book. There's a constant sense that something is wrong, that disaster waits at every turn. The plotting feels haphazard, but I got the sense that it was purposeful. Whether or not this was a choice on the author's part, it worked well for me. <br /><br />Admittedly, the first half is a little slow, but the twists come so fast you're left reeling. I liked the balance between action and character development. <br /><br />While this isn't a YA suspense standout like <i>Dangerous Girls</i> or <i>Genuine Fraud</i>, it's certainly a well-done novel. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3363192041110852346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1997599537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5278567009551701176">“Sometimes the kindest thing you can do for a person is to shield them from that which will not help them. Make the decision and then carry the burden yourself, bear the weight so that they don't have to.” <br/>― Lynn Weingarten, Suicide Notes from Beautiful Girls<br/><br/><br/><br/>I read alot of YA and many a mystery too. This was not the worst but I did not understand alot of it and certain parts actually made me a bit queasy. So that is why I did not like it.<br/><br/>SPOILERS:<br/><br/>There was so much I did not get nor understand. I</span>
  <span id="freeText5278567009551701176" style="display:none">“Sometimes the kindest thing you can do for a person is to shield them from that which will not help them. Make the decision and then carry the burden yourself, bear the weight so that they don't have to.” <br />― Lynn Weingarten, Suicide Notes from Beautiful Girls<br /><br /><br /><br />I read alot of YA and many a mystery too. This was not the worst but I did not understand alot of it and certain parts actually made me a bit queasy. So that is why I did not like it.<br /><br />SPOILERS:<br /><br />There was so much I did not get nor understand. I also felt the tone of the book was not for me.<br /><br />I really feel like this is not a traditional mystery or psychological thriller. I feel it is more geared toward the Horror/thriller genre. I most likely would not have chosen to read it had I known how brutal and..well..horrifying it would be. I think it does work though as a horror tale because it sure is a creepy little read! And somehow I made it to the end so I was at least kept involved. Not my type of book though at all.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1422107265?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacquelyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacquelyn" href="/user/show/7822663-jacquelyn">Jacquelyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781481418539" href="/book/show/23309655-suicide-notes-from-beautiful-girls">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1422107265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10302777145766805039">Hmm. When starting this, I thought I was going to love it. The writing was great and the story had me captivated. However, after the halfway mark, the book took a different spin and I didn't really enjoy it as much. Also, I was a little thrown off when we started having more than one point of view. I thought that in the beginning, the pacing was great but when we began reading from multiple points of views, the pacing was was thrown off a bit. Also, I was ready to have my mind blown but it didn'</span>
  <span id="freeText10302777145766805039" style="display:none">Hmm. When starting this, I thought I was going to love it. The writing was great and the story had me captivated. However, after the halfway mark, the book took a different spin and I didn't really enjoy it as much. Also, I was a little thrown off when we started having more than one point of view. I thought that in the beginning, the pacing was great but when we began reading from multiple points of views, the pacing was was thrown off a bit. Also, I was ready to have my mind blown but it didn't really happen. I don't know whether everyone felt this way but I finished the book still confused as to what had really happened. I hate that. I just read this whole book to figure out and uncover what happened and I close the book still confused as to what happened. Although I am not sure if I fully understand the ending, I really did enjoy what I did grasp and understand. I didn't like that part of it but I must say, the writing was great and it flowed really nicely. This was an odd one for me. I liked about 60% of it but the other 40% was just bleh for me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10302777145766805039" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sf9w0qVSEcN1Gw3MVCp7Br05Rjl87lOtGRN/aHwFb/Uzr4q7PDBeZKGe+cL6EH+7dzE7B7F2OQ8SjEVnajfcZA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer456720312309093030">Lynn Weingarten is a New York Times bestselling author living in Brooklyn. Her fifth young adult novel, BAD GIRLS WITH PERFECT FACES, was released in the US on Halloween 2017. It will be out in the UK on January 11th, 2018. <br/><br/>Her previous books include SUICIDE NOTES FROM BEAUTIFUL GIRLS (a NY Times bestseller, a YALSA Teens’ Top Ten book for 2016, one of Vanity Fair’s list of Best Books for July, an</span>
  <span id="freeText456720312309093030" style="display:none">Lynn Weingarten is a New York Times bestselling author living in Brooklyn. Her fifth young adult novel, BAD GIRLS WITH PERFECT FACES, was released in the US on Halloween 2017. It will be out in the UK on January 11th, 2018. <br /><br />Her previous books include SUICIDE NOTES FROM BEAUTIFUL GIRLS (a NY Times bestseller, a YALSA Teens’ Top Ten book for 2016, one of Vanity Fair’s list of Best Books for July, and on The Guardian’s list of 5 of the Best in Young Adult Fiction), and WHEREVER NINA LIES (an ALA Top Ten Popular Paperback for Young Adults, a New York Public Library Book for the Teen Age, a YALSA Teen’s Top Ten Nominee and a Sequoyah Book Award Nominee) <br /><br />In the past, Lynn edited books and developed ideas for Alloy Entertainment. She is currently Creative Director of Dovetail Fiction, a new sister company from the book packager Working Partners.<br /><br />She can be found on Twitter and Instagram as @lynnweingarten</span>
